Problem with Education Fees in Hebei; Education Department Reduces and Distributes Funding to Colleges and Universities; Education Federation Sends Representatives to Petition Song Zheyuan

(Special Dispatch from Hebei) Due to the Hebei Education Department's reduction of education fees for the 25th year for Hebei provincial middle schools and above in Pingjinbao, it is difficult to maintain operations. Previously, a request was made to the Jicha Political Committee to avoid the reduction, but no approval has been received. The Education Department also stated that it has not received a clear order and will still implement the original resolution. Therefore, a problem has arisen with education fees. As the start of the school year is imminent, each college and university has sent representatives, including Yang Shaozhou and ten others, representing the Pingjinbao Provincial College and University Faculty and Staff Federation, to Pingjin to petition Song Zheyuan and submit a presentation outlining the difficult situation. Details of the situation from each party are as follows:

Presentation to Song Zheyuan

We respectfully note that in order to ensure that the revenue and expenditure of the province's budgeted income and expenditure for the 25th year are balanced, it was proposed to reduce and distribute education funding. Colleges and universities believe that education is a long-term plan for cultivating talent and should be developed step by step. It should not be abandoned due to minor setbacks. We have repeatedly submitted requests to maintain the original state. We also invited Vice President Li Shuhua, President Li Zheng, President Li Linyu, President Mei Yiqi, Professor Shu Xuan of Yenching University, Dean Zhou Xuezhang, Dean Li Jianxun, and other education leaders to represent the position of upholding education in this province and to provide clarification and request subsidies. We were gratified to receive a sincere reply from Chairman Song, stating that the reduced distribution refers to inflated education expenses and not the reduction of school funding. We admire Chairman Song's consistent commitment to education. Since we have received this promise, which is as weighty as the words of a tripod, we should quietly await its implementation. However, the supervisor has not received a clear order, and the government departments have no way to follow it. Now that the start of the school year is approaching, we have inquired in Baoding but have not received any definitive information. Faculty and staff in each school are panicking and feeling uneasy. If this uncertainty continues, it may affect the spirit of education. As faculty and staff, we feel a sense of crisis and dare not remain silent. We have publicly selected representatives to come to your office to request that you promptly order the provincial government to implement the previously communicated decision to the educational leaders in order to prevent the entire province's education from falling into a desperate situation. A solid education can stabilize the hearts of the people. During the previous student petition and strike, we relied on the faculty and staff to remain calm and provide advice from the sidelines, which fortunately resolved the crisis. If the start of this year's school year is affected by reduced funding, it will cause educators to feel insecure and shake the students' desire to learn, which could lead to further concerns for the leader and would be unfortunate for the region. The various reasons why education funding should not be reduced have been fully explained in previous submissions from each school president and a recent letter from the faculty and staff. This information has already been carefully reviewed by Chairman Song, so we will not repeat it. However, we believe it is important to note that the original plan includes measures such as eliminating departments and merging departments and reducing the number of schools. However, the actual savings will be limited. Moreover, the field of aquatic products is related to the recovery of coastal fishing rights and the development of important production in the province, which is crucial to the nation's survival and the people's livelihood. The Aquatic Products College has recently achieved significant results. If it is instructed to actively promote this field, the gains will be substantial. Compared with the current reduction in minimal funding, the gains and losses cannot be reasonably calculated. The departments set up in the Law and Commerce and Women's Normal schools have all been established in consideration of social needs. How can we abandon something due to minor setbacks? Chairman Song is currently recruiting university graduates, and all disciplines such as literature, science, law, and engineering are included, demonstrating that all types of talents are needed. If we hastily abandon a part of a school with a long history and a proven track record due to temporary financial difficulties, it will require twice the effort to restore it in the future. All of this should be carefully considered to avoid reductions. According to our limited knowledge, we have prepared a brief summary for your review. If there are any omissions, the representatives can provide further explanation during the audience. Respectfully submitted to Chairman Song of the Jicha Political Committee. Submitted by the Faculty and Staff Federation of Colleges and Universities in Pingjinbao.

Petition Situation

The Faculty and Staff Federation of Colleges and Universities in Pingjinbao selected one representative from each college and university to come to Pingjin. The representatives included Yang Shuping from Tianjin Institute of Technology, Zhu Zhengsu from Tongxian Women's Normal School, Wang Youmin from Hebei High School, Zhai Peiqi from Tongxian Men's Normal School, Shao Shangzhi from Baoding Medical College, Dr. Cao from Tianjin Middle School, Yi Shufen from Tianjin Law and Commerce College, Tian Yi'an from Tianjin Aquatic Products School, Li Shengqiao from Tianjin Women's Normal College, Wang Zeli from Baoding Senior Vocational School, Song Guozhen from Baoan Women's Normal School, Li Hefang from Baoding Men's Normal School, Han Fengzhai from Baoding Middle School, and Cheng Yaofeng from Tianjin Normal School. On the morning of the 29th, at 10:30 am, they went to the Jicha Political Committee to petition. Chairman Song Zheyuan had gone to Nanyuan to inspect the military. The representatives requested to meet with Yang Zhaogeng, Director of Political Affairs, but Mr. Yang was also busy and unable to meet. Wang Shichen from the Administrative Office relayed the message on his behalf. Director Yang stated that he was unable to provide a specific response and still needed to consult with Chairman Song for a final decision. He agreed to visit Song in Nanyuan that afternoon to discuss effective solutions. The representatives left the summary they had brought with Director Yang and briefly explained the key points of their request. They then left. It is reported that they will visit the Political Committee again on the morning of the 31st to present everything in person. (Jin)

Lung Examination of Elementary School Teachers Began Yesterday

In order to prevent the spread of pulmonary tuberculosis among children, the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association has given X-ray lung examinations to elementary school teachers in this city, starting yesterday. Registration for the Municipal General Examination Begins; Examination Types Divided into Six Categories; Registration Location is at the Municipal Education Bureau

The Municipal Education Bureau is holding the municipal general examination, and registration began yesterday. This examination is divided into six types: general administrative personnel, financial administrative personnel, health administrative personnel, police administrative personnel, teacher administrative personnel, and construction personnel. The registration deadline is the 30th of this month, and the examination will begin on November 1st. The eligibility requirements are: (1) Graduates from public or registered private secondary schools or above who have certificates, or (2) Those who have equivalent academic qualifications to graduates from secondary schools or above and have passed the qualification examination. The registration procedures are: (1) Fill out a registration resume, (2) Submit qualification certificates and three recent 4-inch half-length photos, (3) Provide a guarantor's guarantee letter, and (4) Pay a registration fee of one yuan. The guarantor should be a current civil servant above the level of assignment, a current party affairs worker above the level of assistant cadre in the central party headquarters, provincial party headquarters, special municipal party headquarters, or overseas general branch, or a current principal or teacher of a secondary school or above or a elementary school principal. However, staff involved in the examination process cannot be guarantors. All types of examinations, except for construction personnel and health administrative personnel, which are divided into two tests, are divided into three tests. The scoring method is as follows: for three tests, the first test accounts for 40%, the second test accounts for 40%, and the third test accounts for 20%; for two tests, the first test accounts for 70% and the second test accounts for 30%.

Finance: Central Bank Opens for Cash, Gold Price Rises by $1.80

Yesterday's gold market saw pure gold rise. The market opened slightly better, and later, there were frequent openings for cash, gradually becoming brisk. As a result, it rose by $1.80. Early morning reports indicated that the overseas silver market was flat in both England and the United States. Sources claimed that after the market closed, the posted prices had buyers, with India and the U.S. Treasury Department on the buying side, and China and speculators on the selling side. Forward silver prices in Mont de Piété rose between five cents and one and eight-tenths of a cent. Exchange rates rose slightly, and London raw gold rose by half a penny. The Central Bank announced its posted rates, which were flat for both England and the United States. The customs gold unit remained unchanged. The standard gold bar price rose to $1124.20. The informal pre-market trading opened at $6.34. Although Demao Yong sold, Fuxing Yong, Qiafeng Yong, and others were active. The morning opened with high prices, and large investors bought, continuing the rise. The HSBC Bank announced its posted rates, which were flat for both England and the United States. At this point, there was a slight downturn, but large investors still had strong appetites for buying, and there were continued rumors of the Central Bank opening for cash. Although the silver equalization tax was not changed, the trend was steady. The market was quite firm at noon, and the outlook remained prosperous. However, because sellers took advantage of the high prices, Indian silver initially rose by twenty-three annas, and then again by one anna. It fell back at one point, but buyers still flooded in, and the market closed firm. The day's market conditions are recorded below.

The morning opening was $1126.80, $0.30 better than the previous close. Futai Heng and Futai Yong, Tongfeng Heng, and others raised the price to $7.40. The HSBC Bank announced its posted rates, which were flat for both England and the United States. Later, Qian Changxiang and others sold slightly, lowering the price to $6.90. Futai Yong, Dade Cheng, and Dachang Xiang bought bars. Although the silver equalization tax announcement was flat, rumors of the Central Bank's withdrawal of cash from official accounts boosted sentiment, and the price gradually rose to $8.00. The noon close was $1127.90.

The afternoon market opened at $1127.90. Hengmao Yong and Qiafeng Yong, Chengda, and others bought bars, raising the price to $8.30. Yuanmao Yong and Qiafeng Yong, Chengda sold off, falling to $8.30. Hongkang, Qian Changxiang, Fuxing Yong, Chunyuan Yong, and others were prepared to buy, gradually pulling the price up. The closing price was $1128.30.

The settlement price, according to the Central Bank's standard gold bar price, was posted at $1124.20, about $4 more than the closing price. The book price for this month was $1125, and for October, $1128. Morning replenishment water was $1125. Red gold was increased by $8 to $1134.80. The spot market was peaceful. Tianjin goods were increased by $12.75. Refined red gold selling price was $14.50, buying price was $11, but there were no counterparties. The forward market initially saw Duofang Xianghe eager to post, and posted seven bars to Shengyuan Yong, at $2.80. Later, Jingfu and others were willing to post in at $2.50, but there were still no counterparties.

Trading in the market was normal. In summary, Shengyuan, Wanxing, Tongfeng, Hengda, Dachang Xiang, Futai Yong, Fuyu, Chunyuan Yong, and others were on the buying side. Hengyu, Dade Cheng, Qingfa Yong, Qian Changxiang, Fuda, Qiafeng Yong, Yuanmao Yong, Futai Yong, Chengda, and others were on the selling side. Shenda Yong advanced first and then exited, and Qian Changxiang exited first and then advanced.

An examination of the day's market conditions shows a shift from flat to stable. The market opened at $1126.80 and closed at $1128.30, representing the day's highest and lowest prices, with a fluctuation of $1.50. As a result, it rose by $1.80 compared to the previous close. There were 679 bars remaining for this month, with nine long positions and six short positions. There were a total of 8757 chips for October, with thirty long positions and forty short positions. The total volume traded was 1274 bars in the morning market and 756 bars in the afternoon market.

Foreign Exchange Remains Unchanged, Foreign Banks Sell Off... Shanghai Maintains

Yesterday, although foreign banks sold off in the foreign exchange market, Shanghai managed to maintain stability. Early morning reports indicated that London cable transfers, both near and far, were flat. Sources claimed that after the market closed, the posted prices had buyers, with India and the U.S. Treasury Department buying, and China and speculators selling. The New York silver market remained unchanged. Forward silver prices in Mont de Piété rose between five cents and one and eight-tenths of a cent. London raw gold rose by half a penny. The British pound rose against the U.S. dollar by 1.25, and against the French franc by one pound. The U.S. dollar rose against the British pound by 1.25, and against the French franc by 1.875. The Central Bank announced its posted rates, which were flat for both England and the United States. The customs gold unit remained unchanged. The foreign exchange market opened with recent selling prices, with the British pound quoted at 1 shilling, 2 pence, 3125 and 375/10000, and the U.S. dollar quoted at $30.125 and $30.1875, compared to the previous close. Overall, there were no major changes in the British pound or the U.S. dollar. After opening, although foreign banks sold off shillings, Shanghai maintained. The HSBC Bank announced its posted rates, which were flat and stable for both England and the United States. Later, although the silver equalization tax was flat, Mobil Oil came to settle near and far U.S. dollar contracts, improving the situation slightly. Sentiment in the afternoon market was calmer, and trading was limited. Indian silver initially rose by twenty-three annas, and then again by one anna, but the overall trend remained unchanged. By the close, the recent selling prices were with the British pound quoted at 1 shilling, 2 pence, 375 and 40625/100000, and the U.S. dollar quoted at $30.125 and $30.1875, compared to the previous close. Overall, both the British pound and the U.S. dollar were flat. The same was true for forward contracts. Shanghai had relatively strong buying appetite. The day's transactions are recorded below.

The British pound opened in the morning with a recent selling price of 1 shilling, 2 pence, 40625/100000. Citibank, Great Britain, and Hua Bi sold to Shanghai November contracts at 34375/100000. Securities: Government Bonds Remain Stagnant, Market Trading Also Very Quiet

Yesterday, the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange saw extremely stagnant and range-bound market conditions. Both long and short positions largely stood aside and watched. Most retail investors were almost entirely absent from the market, mainly because, before the environment becomes clearer, it will likely remain in a stagnant and range-bound state. Throughout yesterday, there was really no trend to speak of. Apart from two or three that did not fluctuate at all, the opening prices of the rest were mostly slightly better by five cents to one dime. Type Wu was also up by two and a half dimes because it was uniquely small the day before. Since then, trading in each session has become increasingly quiet, and market prices have become increasingly flat. A considerable number of sessions saw absolutely no rise or fall. Even when there were ups and downs, they only jostled with each other within a range of five cents or one dime. Although there were calls for large trades, very few were actually executed, so even a transaction of thirty to fifty thousand was enough to attract attention. It is feared that it will not be easy to break the dull situation for the time being. As a result, only the June 96 and Type Ding bonds fell slightly by five cents to one and a half dimes this month. The rest continued to rise by nine cents to one dime, or two dimes. The total transaction volume was $2.69 million. The results of the rise and fall are listed in the table below. Yarn and Cotton: Spot Sales Active, Tagged Yarn Still Declines... Influence of Falling Raw Cotton

The yarn market rose in the morning and fell in the afternoon. Initially, spot sales were strong and American cotton rebounded, causing some shorts to cover. However, ultimately, due to the weak trend in raw cotton, it fell back again. Nevertheless, spot demand was quite active, due to the interest of Yunnan, Changsha, and other buyers from inland areas, causing the yarn market to decline (affected by cotton). February futures yarn was listed today, with a rumored opening price of $199.70.

Tagged Yarn Initially Rises, Then Falls

The tagged yarn market opened in the morning, with American cotton firm due to buying by the same industry and short covering. Prices rose by three to six pounds. Furthermore, due to continued activity in spot yarn sales after yesterday evening's close, over 600 bales of large-hair ten-count October futures and over one hundred bales of seventeen-count futures were traded. Market sentiment was therefore boosted, and prices for each month rose by $0.80 to $1. However, as Dafu, Hengyi, Yuda, Runkang, and other firms sold out, prices gradually declined after the second session. As a result, it was similar to yesterday's close. This month's futures remained unchanged, while near and far futures rose by only $0.10 to $0.30. The market was still stable after opening in the afternoon. Suddenly, in the second session, the trend of loose selling on the raw cotton counter became prevalent, and the decline became more pronounced at the third close. As a result, prices fell by $1.10 to $2.20 compared to the morning close. It was found that sellers included Dafu (2,350 bales), Tongji (1,250 bales), Hengyi (2,750 bales), Yuda (1,450 bales), Jinchang (1,600 bales), Gengfeng (1,800 bales), Renfeng (900 bales), Xingchang (1,350 bales), Yichengchang (800 bales), Runkang (2,700 bales), and Xiesheng (1,600 bales). Both Longs and Shorts are Selling, Tagged Cotton Plunges by Seventy Cents

The cotton market rose in the morning and fell in the afternoon. As soon as the market price rose slightly, people began to sell. It was also heard that some longs, seeing the deteriorating environment, painfully closed out their positions. Therefore, the market declined very rapidly. February tagged cotton opened for auction this morning at $38.90. The afternoon closing price was $38.20. It is said that it fell sharply by seventy cents in one day.

The tagged cotton market opened in the morning, with Indian cotton flat, American cotton rebounding by three to six pounds, and the yarn market rebounding, boosting sentiment. October to December rose by two dimes to two and a half dimes. Far futures were flat. After the second session, Dafu, Yuda, Hexing, Huamao, Chongan, and other firms successively sold out. American Cotton Prices Fluctuate... Closing Remains Firm

Yesterday, American cotton opened with each month rising by one to four pounds. Initially, traders, seeing cotton farmers hedging, did not dare to act. However, as traders bought at limit prices, and speculators expected government reports to show a decrease, and that arid areas lacked sufficient moisture, and that Texas had excessive rainfall, there was also considerable buying, and prices rose. Before the close, as hedging increased, some experienced reaction. However, traders and Wall Street still bought, spot demand was sluggish, and some offset previous amounts. The close was firm. It is estimated that spot prices rose by six pounds, and futures rose by three to six pounds. British cotton spot prices fell by one point, and futures rose by four to five points. Indian cotton initially rose due to buying by operators, but weakened due to selling by European exporters. Traders awaited crop reports for Indian and British cotton. It is estimated that Pingguoer fell by half a rupee, Oumula fell by 0.25 rupees, and Bairuoxi rose by 0.75 rupees. Raw electricity is recorded on the left. (Cable from the 31st)

Piece Goods: Hebei-Chahar Reduces Import Duties, Northbound Sales of Cotton Cloth Suddenly Stagnate, Central China Also Affected

Yesterday, the cotton cloth market saw a slight return to calm for East Goods because the sharp decline at the end of July had just passed, and month-end deliveries had been completed. The decline in domestic fine cloth, fine twill, and coarse cloth was relatively moderate. Yesterday, there was a continued decline, with each bolt falling by several cents to one dime. Printed and finished dyed cloths all trended uniformly weak. This was mainly because raw cotton was still difficult to stabilize. Several Shanghai-Hankou Chinese factories and Japanese textile mills in Tianjin all resumed operations one after another, and production will increase day by day. Today's announcement of Hebei-Chahar's reduction of import duties means that not only will Chinese goods shipped to the two provinces of Hebei-Chahar be crowded out, but Central China will also be affected. Therefore, the purchase of printed straight-grain, serge, satin, colored serge, melton, all kinds of light and heavy coarse cloth, etc. by the Tianjin group before last week was very active. In recent days, it has become withered. After a series of market weaknesses, the interest of each road has become increasingly faint. The Sichuan group's orders for blue cloth, straight-grain, serge, printed velvet, are still numerous. Shaanxi, Henan, Shanxi, and Shandong various plain and printed straight-grain serge white velvet printed velvet new flower flannel crepe de chine have good purchase appetites, and over 300 pieces were brought in yesterday. Due to the uncertainty of the Guilin situation in Yunnan and Guangdong, the market inventory is exhausted, and there is considerable buying interest. Selling offers are very harsh, and activity is slow. About 400 pieces of fine twill, fine cloth, straight-grain, serge, and flannel were brought in yesterday. The Yangtze River group and inland groups are all waiting and watching due to poor market conditions. There are many telegrams to postpone the handling of trust shipments.

Silk and Tea: Ningzhou Black Tea Sales to England Still Smooth

Yesterday, the road for Ningzhou black tea to England was still not lonely. The entire city was bought by Jardine Matheson & Co. for over 500 boxes, with prices ranging from $28.50 to $33. Jardine Matheson & Co. also had scattered negotiations for Qimen black tea with Jinlong and Tongfu. The market is already brewing. As for the green tea market, it was still the same as yesterday. The trading of drawn-core Zhenmei green tea was quite smooth. Tunxi famous brand Gaozhuang goods again opened to a top price of $128. Weishi Gaozhuang, on account of Chunzhu tea, opened to a top price of $130. The market for goods with excellent quality and manufacturing methods suddenly became sharp. However, due to the abundance of low-zhuang inferior goods in the market, the market price still has no chance to rise.

According to a report from the Tea Industry Association, the green tea market is quiet because various firms are proceeding with matching piles to prepare for the departure of tea ships for Morocco. However, about 1,000 boxes of Yushan Zhenmei, which Xiehe negotiated the day before, at a price of $40, were officially traded yesterday, and Jardine Matheson took in more than 600 boxes of tea from the two Lakes, at a price of $29.75. The tea is still in Hankou and is now being telegraphed to be shipped to Shanghai.

North and South Goods: Tong'an Dried Longan Meat Has Arrived in Shanghai

The first batch of new Tong'an Guiyuan meat. It was discovered that on the day before yesterday, the Jinan ship entered the port, and over 30 boxes had already been transported, with Changsheng Dexing, Dongchun Defeng, Jicheng, and other brands all having stock on hand. The samples were seen yesterday, and the goods are still red and bright, and the body is also dry. It is said that the cost is more than ten yuan higher than sea transport. However, recently, the price of Lianzhou Guiyuan meat has been falling, so the market trend seems difficult to sell well. It is estimated that the market will open today.

The New White Lotus Market Has Stabilized

Since the emergence of new white lotus seeds, the market has felt depressed due to the softening of production prices. According to recent letters from Lanxi, processing prices have slightly improved, and the market has stabilized. Therefore, the Shanghai market is also trending towards stability. Yesterday, the market price was called at $36-37.

Metals: Eastern Steel Plates Arrive in China One After Another

Recently, Japanese merchants have been studying hardware products with great care, so recently, such as Shin Yangyuan, I-beams, black iron sheets, Shin Pan Yuan, angle iron, etc., all have the intention of selling their products. Recently, steel plates have also arrived in China. It was discovered that yesterday and today, such as Mitsubishi, Dagu, and Huishan, all had large quantities of spot goods arriving, which had a considerable impact on the Western goods market.

Special Report

Hankou New Soybean Prices Reduced to Encourage Sales

Yesterday, new early yellow soybeans from Hankou, due to abundant supply and sluggish sales, led sellers to reduce prices to boost sales. As a result, oil mills purchased 5,600 to 5,700 bags, causing prices to plummet by 30 to 50 cents. Jiujiang and Changzhou soybeans were also slightly affected. The sales market remained fragmented, with Fuzhou and Guangdong merchants on this street purchasing 1,300 to 1,400 bags of various Jiujiang soybeans, and over 500 bags of Changzhou cowhide yellow soybeans. Stored soybeans, which had been quiet for a long time, finally moved, with factories buying four truckloads of Bengbu soybeans at prices ranging from 5.70 to 5.65 yuan. Shen Bao National Goods Special Publication

The Attitude of Bank Clerks Should Be Like This (?)

— Xi Nan

In recent years, various banks in Shanghai have established branches and offices in areas where local commerce is relatively prosperous and residents are relatively well-off, whether in the eastern or western districts. This is certainly convenient for the general public's deposits, but it is actually done with the intention of expanding their own business. According to future trends, if banks can handle deposit and withdrawal procedures to everyone's satisfaction, who would be willing to keep cash at home and bear the risks themselves? Moreover, putting money in the bank offers some interest, so why not do it?

However, the way current banks treat their customers is really not praiseworthy. Among them, there are indeed many who provide attentive service and handle matters quickly. But there are also many who seem to think that all the gold and silver in the bank are their personal property. They display an air of arrogance, reeking of money, treating customers with indifference. They leisurely read newspapers, put their feet up while chatting, appearing completely unhurried, letting you wait anxiously and stand until your legs ache. The clerk always acts slowly, looking around distractedly. If you urge them a bit, they will glare at you and even mock you. Therefore, some people say that walking into a bank is like walking into a cold storage room, with a chilling atmosphere that makes people uncomfortable. How can customers be treated like this? It only happens with a few bank clerks who lack service ethics and don't value themselves.

The important figures in the bank don't bother to manage these things. In fact, the reason why clerks dare to act like this is because they are following the example set by their superiors. The arrogant attitude they display towards the clerks daily is then passed on by the clerks to the customers. They think this is the proper attitude for a bank employee, and that anything less would not befit their status. Clerks, for the sake of their livelihood, must endure the arrogance of their superiors, which is understandable. But customers are truly the source of their livelihood, yet they are met with scorn. It's a reversal of cause and effect, and a cause for叹息.

Nowadays, quite a few banks, in order to develop their business, collect tuition fees and pay salaries on behalf of others. This spirit of serving the community is deeply admirable. However, the reality is not always as good as it seems. There are indeed banks that handle these matters thoroughly, but many only know how to grab business without making any preparations themselves. When the dates for collection and payment arrive, many people crowd outside the counters, but their response is still limited to handling the usual few customers. No matter how frantically they work, they can't cope. In the end, it only tires out those paying tuition fees or receiving salaries, wasting their efforts. Urging them is ineffective, and there's no way to reason with them. It's all due to the incompetence of the bank manager. If you want the business, you should prepare adequate manpower to handle it. Or, you could stagger the collection and payment dates to save labor. You should also consider the needs of those making payments and receiving money. If they are made to wait a long time, wouldn't that disrupt their affairs? However, these considerations are not within the bank manager's plans. They want to do business, but they don't care about the difficulties and convenience of customers. Alas, such are bank clerks.

Therefore, if banks want to develop their business, they shouldn't think that customers can be treated however they like. If you don't train your clerks and urge them to correct their mistakes and strive for improvement, then no matter how strong your credit is, people will surely leave you with disappointment. At that time, you will be able to catch sparrows with a net, which is the result you should expect from poor customer service.

Page 18

Grain: Factories Selling Short... Spot Sales Stagnant, Marked Flour Market Weak, February Has Also Opened, Prices Steadily Declining

Yesterday, in the flour market, after the opening in the morning, prices for all months showed a pattern of first stabilizing and then falling. Quotations for foreign wheat remained sluggish, falling by about 0.25 to 0.20 yuan. When the prices opened, buying and selling were very smooth, as if the forces were evenly matched, so the market atmosphere was still stable. Later, however, factories successively sold short, and spot flour sales did not show vigorous activity. People's hearts thus became uniformly weak. The stock exchange market is primarily based on people's sentiment. If they are optimistic, they expect great success; if they are pessimistic, they are indifferent and lifeless. Therefore, wheat production remains the same, but the surrounding environment has changed drastically. Fearing that actual sales will not keep up, there is still pressure to lower prices. When the market opened in the afternoon, trading was lighter, and the market, while fluctuating, still showed signs of weakness. February has also opened as usual, with an initial price of 3.265 yuan, steadily weakening, and closing at 0.24 yuan, also down 0.025 yuan, it is said.

Spot Goods Sold Short Recently, Next Month's Wheat Down 0.70 Yuan

Yesterday, in the wheat futures market, after the opening in the morning, prices for all months initially stabilized and then fell. At first, the drop in foreign wheat was minimal, and people's sentiment was stable. However, the flour market turned downwards, and this year's autumn harvest is expected to be bountiful. Since the main food supply is difficult to raise high, people in the industry cannot help but think of this. People's hearts relaxed, selling pressure gradually increased, and the market generally fell back down. When the market opened in the afternoon, the near-term market remained sluggish because the factories' appetite for spot wheat was not as strong as it was several weeks ago. Therefore, the spot goods of merchants were sold short in the near term, making the market atmosphere even more gloomy, and the decline was greater than in the distant months. February has also opened, with an initial price of 5.30 yuan, and the closing price was 0.03 yuan better. In the spot wheat market, factories are naturally cautious due to the decline in flour sales. It is said that high-quality goods are discounted as much as 0.90 yuan before factories are willing to buy.

Rice Prices Initially High, Then Moderately Revised Down, Dongxin Japonica Alone Rises by 0.20 Yuan

(South Shanghai) Yesterday, various gangs arrived with a total of fourteen or fifteen boats, carrying over three thousand dan of goods. However, sales in this street market still struggled to recover. Only the Weihaiwei gang sold over two hundred packages. Therefore, although the prices of thick and thin rice were stable, medium-quality rice saw varying degrees of depreciation. Duyang tip and Yinbian Yuanping were mediocre. Dongxin's supplies were intermittently reduced due to alternating overcast and rainy weather, and its price alone rose by 0.20 yuan. New tip rice, however, was just as it was.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, over ten boats arrived from various gangs downstream. The market had varied demand: white japonica, sheep tip, and new customer tip were still active; thin rice was average; and the remaining goods were quite sluggish. Market prices: high-quality white japonica were stable, medium-quality and lower-quality rice held steady, thin rice, sheep Du and Bu tip prices were stable, Yuan rice prices were down by 0.03 to 0.04 yuan, new customer tip was up nearly 0.10 yuan, and Dongxin japonica was up 0.20 yuan.

Advocating for the Domestic Automobile Industry

— Xuan Wan

The development of domestic industry is naturally proportional to the progress of transportation construction. In the past, the obstruction of transportation in various parts of our country greatly hindered the promotion and sales of domestic products to the inland, which greatly affected the development of the entire domestic industry.

However, in recent years, national highways have been completed one after another, with over 90,000 kilometers already open to traffic, and over 30,000 kilometers still being planned and constructed. The sales of domestic products to the inland have therefore followed the development of transportation construction and have become much more convenient. However, because our country does not yet have its own automobile industry and relies entirely on imports, it causes huge financial losses every year, and at the same time, it has also created a serious problem of the outflow of economic rights.

Recently, I heard a very gratifying piece of news, that is, industrialists in our country have recognized this and initiated the establishment of the China Automobile Manufacturing Company, with a capital of six million yuan. It is planned to establish the main factory in Wuzhou, Hunan, and a branch factory in Shanghai. Within two years of starting production, it will produce one hundred vehicles per month, and within five years, it will be able to manufacture all parts itself, providing low-priced goods for domestic use. The establishment of this new enterprise can not only recover economic rights, but is also important to our entire industry. It is a major prerequisite for the current national economic construction.

Here, we can also think of the invention of the charcoal car, which is also a major achievement in our country's industry. Judging from the results of the experiments, the performance is excellent, and the fuel consumption is extremely low. Therefore, we hope that the entire industrial sector will actively promote and manufacture them together, so that China's current transportation construction and the entire national industry can be advanced to a newer and higher stage.

In short, at present, we must integrate the transportation construction industry with the development of domestic products. Only through the development of the domestic automobile industry can we recover financial losses and stimulate and prosper industry and commerce. Only through the progress of transportation construction can the transportation of domestic products be facilitated, so that domestic products can penetrate into the border provinces and the remote areas of the country.

Contribution

How to Interview Housewives?

— Yang An

Housewives are the main consumers of domestic goods. If housewives are enthusiastic about domestic goods, the path for domestic goods will naturally be unobstructed. However, how to open up this path is the task of female interviewers. The other day, I heard the speeches of twenty-five volunteers who were acting as female interviewers, and I felt that they were all valuable and had rich experience, so they could be worthy of this position. Based on their opinions, it can be summarized into eight points, which are good references for promoting domestic goods:

(1) It is not advisable to interview housewives after 10 am, because they are about to prepare meals. If you chatter away, you will not only get no results, but also annoy people.

(2) When you meet a housewife, you should not start by directly promoting domestic goods. You must adapt to the situation, not write rigidly, and not speak in platitudes. Look at the current situation and make appropriate remarks. For example, if you see that the housewife is sick, you can talk about the illness. If you see that the housewife is doing needlework, you can talk about sewing experience. If you meet a child, you can talk about education issues. If you meet a female companion, you can talk about domestic issues. In short, engaging conversations are indispensable.

(3) When you meet fashionable housewives, you must not criticize them for not using domestic goods. You should only explain the advantages of domestic goods to them layer by layer so that they can realize it automatically. In particular, you should not talk about being too extravagant or trendy, which will only provoke their anger.

(4) If you meet a stubborn housewife, and one visit is ineffective, you can visit a second time. If she says she doesn't have time today, you can go again tomorrow. Even stubborn stones can nod, and humans will never be permanently unaware.

(5) Housewives all like small advantages. Giving them some discount coupons or samples for them to try may be welcomed by them. In future visits, you can get a lot of results.

(6) When housewives ask us questions, we must first stand in an invincible position. For example, if they ask us if we use domestic goods ourselves, we can declare directly that from head to toe, nothing is not a domestic product. Setting an example is our most important task.

(7) When housewives are unwilling to talk more, we can only say a few simple words or temporarily end the conversation and talk again next time. Talking too much will only make people more disgusted and will certainly not get good results.

(8) It is not advisable to exaggerate, and there is no need to talk about empty words all the time. Be sincere and you may be able to get people to pay attention and adopt our words.

We feel that promoting domestic goods does not require singing high-profile songs or speaking big words. That is, with these eight opinions, female interviewers can do it in practice, and they will definitely get infinite results. Both the interviewer and the interviewee can feel great pleasure.

A Brief Discussion on Shengze Spun Silk

— Jun Mei

The other day, a newspaper reported that since the beginning of summer, many Western women have switched from uncomfortable Western clothing to Chinese-style robes. To be fair, in summer, Chinese clothing is indeed more suitable for the body than Western suits.

Summer clothing is most commonly made of colored silk, and the spun silk produced in Shengze can meet the needs of this season. Now, I will give a brief introduction to its products: There are many types of Sheng silk, including pu, ling, sha, luo, jie, and juan. The most commonly sold and best quality product is naturally the light, new, flowing, white, delicate, and soft spun silk. There are also more than ten types of this kind of spun silk, depending on weight, width, and name. Generally speaking, lighter and narrower fabrics are suitable for making linings, while wider and heavier fabrics are suitable for making shirts or undergarments. Summer clothing, on the other hand, is most durable and economical when made with steel comb spun silk.

Steel comb spun silk comes in two types: electric machine and wood machine. The electric machine type is more uniform. Both are woven with pure natural silk and extremely fine warp threads, so they are very durable and washable. After washing, the color will naturally turn yellowish-pink, which is quite elegant. After wearing it for a long time, and dyeing it a dark color, it is indistinguishable from a newly made garment. Compared to imported Indian silk crepe and other man-made silk blends, which become dull and even develop holes after washing and dyeing, they cannot be compared on the same day.

As for its value, in the place of origin, each bolt is only about thirteen or fourteen yuan. Calculating by five zhang, each foot is less than three jiao. No matter how weak the purchasing power, it is still considered affordable for the common people. However, most of our countrymen only focus on foreign goods as being noble and fashionable, and discard domestic goods, which are more suitable in terms of function and economy, as worthless. Those who wear them also think they are unsophisticated. We hope that our countrymen will strive to eliminate this habit of self-abandonment!

Eliminating Negative Psychology in the Domestic Goods Movement

— Yao Mingran

First, vanity. The word "vanity" is almost always used on women. I often see newspapers, magazines, and monthly publications scolding like this. I certainly can't say that the word "vanity" is used inappropriately, but it is inevitably too focused on women. The world today is a world of equal rights for men and women, so the sanctions on vanity must be jointly responsible for eradicating it. In recent years, the efforts to promote domestic goods have been considerable, but the effectiveness has been meager. Indeed, due to various and multifaceted relationships, the inability to remove vanity is more harmful than the tangible outflow of money. It can simply be said that its latent power is causing the trouble. The only positive way to eliminate it is the joint and practical responsibility just mentioned, and the most easily restrained people are young men and women. If the parents do not sanction the temptation from the outside world, but instead promote and encourage it, they cannot be excused for their guilt. The urgent reform of this kind of psychology is a major event that cannot be delayed!

Second, contempt. It is truly pitiful and laughable to say that the Chinese often despise domestic goods. They think that the promotion of these unique domestic goods texts, records, etc., is ineffective and not worth reading. Indeed, textual propaganda is ineffective, but this can prove the extent of the Chinese people's contempt for domestic goods and their lack of knowledge of domestic goods. They think it's a cliché, and they don't know that the inability of domestic goods to develop, this psychological obstacle, seems insignificant, but in reality, it affects the development prospects of domestic goods, and there is a major crisis. Disasters often arise from subtle things. Fang Xiaoru's famous sentence in "Deep Thoughts" is worth pondering by young and old people. A Western saying is, "Control it by obeying it." Now in such a situation, domestic goods are so declining, we cannot be disappointed and passive, letting it diminish. We must find a way out of the struggle, but to achieve this step, it cannot be done by empty talk. If we do not first defeat such obstacles of domestic goods contempt, I am afraid that there will never be a good way out!

The "hua" character in "xuanhua" (uproar) is mostly written with the "mouth" radical by the world, not with the "speech" radical, becoming the "hua" character, which is a big mistake. Even those of us who play with writing often write "xuanyi" as "xuanhua," which is laughable.

I have a full of blood, intending to sprinkle it on the desolate deserts. I have two lines of tears, wanting to wave them in the time of green wine and red lights.

Modern youths mostly consider film history and dance classics to be compulsory courses.

China Through Foreign Eyes

— Zhu Ying

An American named Mr. Arthur Lee once came to China for a three-month trip. After returning to the United States, he published a travelogue in "American Miscellany." He began by saying that the actual China is different from what we imagined. When we stepped onto the Bund in Shanghai, I almost suspected that this was a large commercial port in the West, and almost did not believe that this was the so-called backward China. All I saw was magnificent buildings and the beauty woven together by modern civilization.

Although the City God Temple in Shanghai is slightly lacking in order, the oriental colors are thicker than anything else. The narrow streets, the old buildings, everywhere shows the Chinese civilization, is history created? The city of Venice is an ancient city in Europe, but in Venice, it is already difficult to see the traces of history, because everything has been transformed into modern times. Egypt and India have mostly buried the civilization of history underground. In the City God Temple in Shanghai, I can see the civilization of the Middle Ages, not the civilization of the Middle Ages that is being performed on the stage and on the screen.

The impression given by Beiping is also very deep. The long hutongs are full of non-lonely quietness. Although living in an old Chinese-style house, lacking all modern living facilities, living in it is very comfortable, which is difficult for people living in the United States to imagine. Beiping has the shell of ancient civilization and the spirit of modern civilization. Its environment is suitable for both yellow and white people? It can be suitable for long-term residence, and also suitable for travel. In short, anyone in Beiping can find a suitable angle that suits them, which is stronger than Guangzhou, Hankou, Tianjin, Qingdao, and even Shanghai does not match the beauty and mystery of Beiping. Moreover, the climate in Beiping is better than in Shanghai, with some flavor of northern Germany.

Although in China, I have also seen the pigtails and small feet mentioned in general travelogues and novels, but not many, and especially the pigtails, I can hardly see them. In China, many women have also cut off their pigtails. Men with pigtails seem to be limited to the two classes of farmers and sedan carriers. Women's small feet seem to be more common, but very few women under the age of forty have small feet, and many have already worn high heels, learned to dance, and imitated the lives of Hollywood actresses. Although transportation in China cannot be said to be extremely developed, in modern China, travelers can use trains and cars to travel seven-tenths of China's vast territory. However, it is said that in China, any dialect is difficult to pass beyond a thousand miles, which is a shortcoming. However, in major cities in various countries, it is possible to contact each other in English without any difficulty.

Establishment of the Wu-Yue History and Geography Research Association

— Wei Juxian

Before recorded history, the Chinese nation migrated from south to north, and culture also migrated from south to north. After recorded history, a part of the nation migrated from north to south, and the cultural artifacts of the south should not be thought of as having migrated from the north. To prove this hypothesis, Neolithic artifacts have been discovered in Jiangnan, which can prove the early culture of Jiangnan. The pottery in the stone tool sites all have geometric patterns, which are completely different from the patterns on pottery in the Yellow River basin during the Stone Age. This can prove that Jiangnan had its own culture, and did not receive the transmission from the north.

The proof of this fact originated from the discovery of stone tools and geometric pattern pottery near Qixia Mountain in Nanjing by the Nanjing Antiquities Preservation Institute in 1930, followed by the discovery of a large number of geometric pottery in Yancheng in Changzhou and Qijiadun in Jinshan. There is the publication of "Visiting Ancient Sites in Yancheng and Jinshan". This aroused everyone's attention. When the Ancient Coin Society was opened in February of this year, Wu Zhihui, Ye Yufu and others discussed the establishment of the Wu-Yue History and Geography Research Association, drafted simple terms, and solicited members. During the preparatory period, Wu City, Yue City, Gusu Terrace, Suiwa Palace, Zuopu pier, and Shaoxing were discovered in Suzhou. A large number of geometric pattern pottery was found, and a large number of stone tools were found in Gudang, Hangzhou. The book "Exploratory Report on the Neolithic Site of Gudang, Hangzhou" was published.

Yesterday, the Wu-Yue History and Geography Research Association held its inaugural meeting in Xuegeng Hall of the Shanghai YMCA at Eight Immortals Bridge. More than 100 people including Cai Yuanpei attended. There were also stone tools from Gudang, Lake Zhou, pottery from Shao, Songjiang, and Jinshan, and porcelain from Yuyao on display. Hundreds of people from all walks of life watched. At the meeting, the articles of association were approved, Cai Yuanpei was elected as the president, Wu Zhihui and Niu Tisheng were elected as the vice presidents, and Yu Youren, Kong Yongzhi, Ye Yufu, and Chen Lifu were elected as councilors. After the association was established, it will of course actively work on the ancient culture of Wu and Yue, but there must be many stone tools and pottery in Jiangsu and Zhejiang that have not yet been discovered. In addition to hiring the directors of the Education Bureau and the directors of the Mass Education Museum in each county in Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces as ex officio members of the investigation committee, they also hired history and geography teachers and Chinese teachers from primary and secondary schools in each county as investigators to investigate local monuments and antiquities. The Wu-Yue History and Geography Research Association will send ten copies of ancient object samples to the education directors of each county in Jiangsu province to send to history and geography teachers and Chinese teachers of various primary and secondary schools for reference. The West Lake Museum will distribute them to the counties in Zhejiang. It is hoped that when stone tools and geometric pattern pottery are encountered in various places, please send a letter to Wei Juxian of the Central Bank of Shanghai so that personnel can be sent to investigate.

Water Crow

— Qing Qu

"Water Crow," that is, a type of crow, but this is a water bird, while the other is a forest bird, which is the main difference. Its color is pure black, shaped like a duck, but larger. At first glance, it seems to have no eyes, but it is not actually without eyes, because the feathers are mixed with the eyelids, so they are not visible. Its nature is to love fish, so fishermen raise them. Those who are good at catching fish are extremely valuable, each head costing twenty or thirty yuan or more, and even ordinary ones cost more than ten yuan. Feeding them is not easy, so water crows are not a breeding species, and those who know them are few.

In my town, the most people who raise water crows are in the Southeast Zhanbang Township and Fei Family Village. Whenever there is a slack in farming, they always use a small boat, holding only a pole in their hand, standing at the stern of the boat, propping it to move forward. Both sides of the boat are water crow houses, numbering more than a dozen heads. Entering the city river, they step on the boat boards with their feet, the sound of which vibrates along the waterfront. Then, they drive the water crow leaders to swim first, and the rest follow in order to compete to enter, disappearing into the water in an instant. The boat moves forward, and the water crows also rush straight ahead. When they encounter a fish, they immediately fight it, catch it, and float up to show their intention to offer a trophy. When the boatman sees this, fearing that they will swallow it, he always uses a pole to hook it, digs the fish out of its beak, and drives it back into the water. Those who catch something are treated in the same way, and the water crows also compete for merit, without slacking off at all. At this time, the fish in the nests on both sides of the bank are startled by the sound, trying to escape and falling into their mouths, none of them can escape. Occasionally, there are huge fish, which are not enough to fight, and they combine their strength to surround them, still fearing they will not win, so they peck at their eyes, first blinding them, and then capture them and lift them up. The courage of the water crow can also be seen.

However, water crows have one characteristic, that is, they lay eggs but cannot incubate them, so they can only take their eggs and have mother chickens work for them. However, after hatching, the chickens abandon them because they are not similar, and they still need human help to grow up. They are fed with mashed small fish and loach every day. They roost in sheds, with horizontal wooden frames to allow them to perch. When they can catch fish, thin money made of twisted grass hearts is first buckled around their necks, so that they cannot swallow the fish, and their two feet are connected with ropes, allowing them to be hooked with a pole. This is why water crows can be tamed and utilized by fishermen. A few days ago, a friend of mine saw this thing and was surprised by it, so he dipped his pen and recorded its outline as above.

Personal Vignettes

The Success Story of Little Star Shirley Temple

— Shadow Stagnant

Seven-year-old Shirley Temple became the most beloved star in Hollywood in 1935. She receives 3,500 fan letters every week. Currently, in the film city, she is considered an important asset by a film company with a capital of US$54 million. She is a short girl, her face looks healthy, but not particularly striking. She had measles once at the age of seven, and soon sent to a dance school in Hollywood, which is the stepping stone for children who want to be on the screen. The dimples on her cheeks are very beautiful, and her yellow hair is curled by her mother's own hands. Initially, she was chosen by a scout from a dance school to play a child role in an educational film. Due to unexpected success, her screen life began. Mrs. Temple was particularly concerned about her daughter at that time, and when she heard that a production company needed a child role, she went to apply. In 1934, Shirley Temple starred in "Little Miss Marker" for Fox Films, and the result was particularly amazing. From then on, she became famous day by day, climbing the path to stardom. However, Hollywood film companies have always treated child stars poorly, and they do not understand the true value of child stars. Therefore, at first, Fox did not pay much attention to Shirley Temple. The first time, they only gave her an unimportant child role in a film. As a result, her success made people realize that she had a special film value. She was worth $190,000, but within three weeks, the income had exceeded the company's estimate. The cost of films starring Shirley Temple is very low, roughly between $200,500 and $000. Apart from the writing of the story, the actors and background props do not seem very important. According to the contract, Shirley Temple makes four films for Fox every year, each earning $75,000. The remaining income of $10,000 per week is contributed by fifteen major companies selling underwear, outerwear, toys, books, puppets, etc., using her photos as trademarks or advertisements. In addition to filming, Shirley Temple is also a broadcasting star in Hollywood. Several of her famous songs have been printed more than 400,000 copies. This number is better than the sales of famous songs by Bing Crosby and Jeanette MacDonald.

At such an age, to be so loved, how is her private life? This is certainly very interesting. In fact, she is a very simple girl, and she obeys her mother in everything. Although she is so young, she is extremely fond of and works hard. She rarely gets sick, and her clothes are not very gorgeous, but very neat. She gets up at seven in the morning, reads the books she read the night before several times, and then goes to the fields to learn dance steps. Her breakfast includes fresh fruit, grains, and boiled eggs. Then she goes to the Fox studio to film with her mother. After work, she returns home and studies various subjects under her mother's supervision. In terms of her level, she seems like a nine-year-old child. She will start learning French next year, and if possible, she may make a film with dialogue in French. At half past five, her day's work is over, she returns home and plays with her father, and then prepares for tomorrow's homework. Her nature is to imitate. When she was filming "Little Lord Fauntleroy," she had to go up and down a 45-foot-high staircase, using dance steps at every turn. It was not easy for the photographer to aim the camera to shoot the film so that every line of the staircase was clearly captured, but the result was not bad, and there were no discrepancies between her steps and the lines of the handrail. She is very happy with her work. When filming, it is as easy as other girls playing with dolls. Because she has sufficient artistic talent, it is easy to train her. Before she starts filming a film, as long as the director explains to her how she should perform in this shot, she understands everything after listening to it once. Not only herself, but also the plays of other actors, she knows. After starting to film, if she makes a mistake, she will immediately ask the photographer to reshoot. When she was filming "Little Lord Fauntleroy," she fell once, falling on the electric light, and once her hand was crushed in the gate. She is a sensitive little girl. When she is holding a doll, if one of the doll's hands accidentally falls off, she will cry, and she will be silent and unhappy for at least half an hour. In the Fox studio, she keeps a few rabbits and chickens, and brings an egg back every day to eat for breakfast the next day. She has collected a lot of her own photos, and in the future, she may become the most famous collector of pictures in the world!

Shirley Temple's success has resulted in her family suddenly becoming wealthy. Now, Mr. Temple has built a new house, with a mountain on one side and a large lawn on the other, to prevent people from looking at Shirley Temple through the windows. She has two older brothers. Mr. Temple's life has recently undergone a change. He has been promoted from a flexible employee to a branch manager in the bank. He is also a short man. Other women often come to him unexpectedly, asking him to attend gatherings, because they want to learn from Mr. Temple, so that their daughters also have the opportunity to become Shirley Temple and be on the screen. However, Mr. Temple refuses all such invitations. Mrs. Temple is also paid $500 a week by Fox for managing Shirley Temple.

Supplement to the Shanghai Shen Bao

Essays

Methods of Warfare Must Be Humane

— Zhou Ge

The "Civil War" in Spain has been going on for over a month since the military rebellion in Morocco on July 18. Not only has the mutual attacks not ceased, but the cruelty of the killings are said to be unprecedented in history.

Originally, war itself is cruel. When a cannon is fired, flesh and blood fly everywhere. A novelist described the situation on the battlefield, saying that hot blood splashes like thousands of red flowers, and in those thousands of red flowers, hands and feet writhe wildly. If you close your eyes and imagine it, you can understand the cruelty of the situation!

Therefore, in its informal mediation in Spain, the British government put forward, among other things, the first measure: "Methods of warfare must be humane." What are humane methods of warfare? Does war have to be humane in order to be like a children's "snowball fight," which does not hurt people and is interesting? However, this kind of "warfare" is clearly something that the imperialist countries do not want, because that would be tantamount to dismantling their own stage!

To say that the methods of warfare must be humane is to kill an enemy in a more "civilized" way. For example, "beheading" is changed to "shooting," shooting is changed to "electric chair," and it is best to change the electric chair to eating "sleeping pills." That is a very humane "method"! However, in acute war, in blind war, this so-called chronic "killing method" is useless! Moreover, even if the killing is done in a "humane" way, a living life is put to death!

Therefore, I say that to make the methods of warfare humane is to fundamentally abolish war. However, to fundamentally abolish war, we still need "war" to eliminate "war"!

Hedgehog

— You Qi

At dusk, when the sun slanted to the west, covering the foot of the western mountain, the remaining sunlight hung on the treetops in the big courtyard. The cicadas were singing, and the foxtail grass on the wall was swaying in the evening breeze.

The courtyard could be described as quite large. In addition to the quadrangle house (note), the area in the middle was square, with dimensions of more than two zhang both lengthwise and widthwise. The ground was paved with large square bricks. Except for the two intersecting paths necessary in front of the doors of the four houses (east, west, north, and south), the rest of the area was divided into four soil ponds, in which some lovely flowers and plants were planted. Moreover, a large grape trellis was erected in front of the south house's door. People could walk underneath, letting the heavy grapes hang down, watching them turn from green to purple. The sight was very much like a large awning (note).

At this time, my grandmother would break into a smiling face, bring out a bamboo bed and small stools, brew a pot of honeysuckle tea, and bring out her water pipe, which she had used for five or six years. Fanning herself, she would load the tobacco silk time and again, and time and again spit the residual ashes into the soil pond.

At the time, among our sisters and brothers, I was the most favored by my grandmother. Therefore, she would let me lie peacefully on the bamboo bed, use a large banana leaf fan to drive away the poisonous mosquitoes, and hum a few inarticulate tunes when she was happy. Gradually, darkness lowered its wings from the sky, along the grape trellis, and sometimes along the base of the wall. Several small animals were crawling, gray-white, with round bodies, not crawling very fast, sniffing the ground with their noses, as if trying to discover something. Perhaps they were already used to it, they were not afraid of people, gradually approaching the bamboo bed--

--Grandma, hedgehog, hedgehog, I said, jumping off the bed, kicking with my foot, and the body curled into a ball, prostrate and unmoving, retracting its head and not daring to come out, the thorns all over its body defending against external harm.

They often walked out in groups, led by the elders. According to grandmother's legend, this animal has some kind of divine aura. The more there are, the more prosperous the place will be, both in terms of population and career. I understand that this was to stop us from harming them. Sometimes I would laugh, there was no resentment between it and me, why would I go harm it?

Out of curiosity, I once asked our tutor, but the answer I got was still very vague. Later, the Zhang family's mother from the next courtyard told me that when hedgehogs get old, their eyes turn red, like rabbits. They are afraid of wild foxes. No matter how tightly they curl up, they cannot withstand a wild fox's urine. The smell is unbearable to them, which quickly takes away their weak lives. So I wondered if human urine would harm them?

Secretly, while my grandmother was napping, I made friends with the younger brothers of the Zhang and Li families, and with small sticks, we searched for the small cross-courtyard where they entered and exited every day. There, besides some scattered bricks and tiles, there was a shed built between the two walls, under which were placed some useless junk. First, we looked at the brick pile, there were no cracks for them to hide in. Then, we rummaged through the junk, and as a result, we found them all hiding under the rotten cotton, sound asleep. The unexpected raid gave them a lot of shock. There were more than a dozen of them, looking at us in panic.

--Let's try peeing on them! I proposed. My little mind had a strange idea, and of course, there would be no objection.

--Who will pee? Needless to say, it was me. So we rolled out a larger one, peeing, peeing, our eyes fixed on its body, but it didn't move. We waited a long time after we finished peeing, and it still didn't move.

--Maybe human urine is not as potent as wild fox urine? This mystery is forever hidden in the depths of my heart.

After that, I was sent into the social furnace. After that, my grandmother died old, and I could no longer find her loving warmth. After that, I left that courtyard, left that hedgehog. In a blink of an eye, eight years have passed since I went to Jiangnan.

In Jiangnan, I can't see that globular animal. Now, the grapes are about to turn red again. Under the grape trellis, at dusk, perhaps that weak life is still active?

Note: Quadrangle house, a northern bungalow, three rooms on each side, forming four sides.

Large awning, that is, a sunshade.

Old Horseman

— Qi Ying

— Mountain Travel Notes, Part 3

When the eastern horizon had just revealed a line of dawn, our group of four set off again, because we planned to reach the foot of the mountain north of Dalong Mountain today to stay overnight. Hurrying along, on the uphill path, we turned our heads from time to time to look back at the small temple in the mountain gorge where we had stayed last night, shrouded in floating mist. The lush green leaves of the sycamore trees covered its entire face, and we could only faintly see its vermilion roof, serene and elegant. This made us deeply feel the nostalgia for this poetic mountain gorge, and we unknowingly slowed down our pace.

After crossing the mountain peak, a flat road suddenly appeared before our eyes. There were one or two tea stalls selling tea on the roadside, so deserted that there was not a single passerby to rest their feet. The proprietresses were all sticking their butts out in front of the stove, making a fire. In one of the tea stalls, an old man was sitting, leisurely smoking a dry tobacco pipe, putting a leg on a long bench, his eyes fixed on the road. At this moment, seeing us walking up the mountain peak, he hurriedly dragged his shoes and ran to us.

"Sirs, sirs, are you going to the foot of the mountain to the north, rushing to Nanchang Prefecture!" The old man asked us urgently, smiling kindly: "Sirs, ride my horses, my horses' steps are steady and fast, they are all young horses, I guarantee you sirs will be satisfied," he gave us a quick glance with eager eyes, seeing that we did not answer, he continued, "Sirs, my horses are grazing in that mountain valley, if you want to ride them, I will go and fetch them immediately!"

This really made us overjoyed. In this deep mountain wilderness

Page 22

On the difficult road, we have walked nearly a thousand miles. Nothing has ever replaced our tired steps. Today, hearing that we can ride horses, we all agreed without question.

The old man led us to sit down in the tea shed, and he ran to let the horses graze. Halfway there, he hurriedly ran back again: "Sirs, sirs, I'll tell you, promise to ride my horses, you must ride my horses, you can take all my money!"

The old man said as if he was worried, ensuring that they would ride his horses, and then the old man ran satisfied to the mountainside!

The wind under the tea shed was as cool as autumn. The sun had just revealed half of its blood-red face at the end of the eastern mountain. A few cicada calls on the treetops, and the barking of dogs occasionally coming from the distant mountainside, increased the loneliness of us walkers.

The proprietress walked up to us with a kind smile, also soliciting her business: "Sirs, drink our tea before you go, it's still early, the water on the stove will boil in a moment!"

The old man released the horses. Halfway up the mountain, we heard the sound of "ding-dong, ding-dong" from the copper bells on the horses' necks. They were several old horses, so thin that only their bones could be seen, as weak as the old man. Before the old man could saddle the horses, we rode off. The old man chased closely beside us, tying the straps on the saddles for us. We only cared about whipping the horses and running, and he fell behind us, panting and shouting, "Sirs, slow down, slow down! The road ahead is not easy to walk, be careful of falling into the valley!"

Finally, his voice became almost weeping: "Sirs, my horses are sick, they are sick!"

We could still hear the proprietress shouting from the tea shed in the distance: "Sirs, drink my tea before you go, it's still early. Old man (calling the old horseman), why are you telling the sirs to leave so early?"

Fat Pig

— Li Jie

This is what often made Qinggen the Leper laugh himself awake from sweet dreams: "Hehehehe… fat pig… fat pig." His wife always nagged him, "You worthless monkey, the pig is fat, but feel your own body, how thin you are, a consumptive ghost! Feeding the pig day and night, filling its pen day and night, see who you're busy for?" These words sometimes also stirred up Qinggen the Leper's sorrow. Because there were already rumors outside that Grandpa A'hu was coming to weigh his pig. Of course, he wouldn't pay cash, but offset old debts. For several years, Qinggen the Leper hadn't raised any pigs. No matter how much Grandpa A'hu pressed him, he couldn't catch him by the braid. This time it would be hard to escape? "If that really happens," A'hu thought, "then more than half a year of effort will be completely in vain…"

At dusk, Qinggen the Leper again sent a full bucket of pig feed that his wife had cooked to the pigsty through the back door. "It seems a bit fatter again?" This became a psychological effect. In fact, his pig had already reached the slaughtering period, and it couldn't get any fatter. Isn't that right? Its belly already hung to the ground, walking like a rolling stone. If there were a mirror in the pigsty, reflecting Qinggen the Leper, who was as thin as firewood, and his fat pig together, perhaps the sadness stirred up by this scene would be even deeper. However, Qinggen the Leper himself was oblivious to this. He used all his strength to pour the bucket of feed into the stone trough, put the empty bucket outside the pigpen fence, took a breath, and sat facing the inside on the pigsty threshold, which protruded like his spine, his lifeless eyes flickering as he began to calculate in his head.

"Selling it to Butcher Dun isn't worth it. First, Mao Lao'san's money isn't easy to get. Second, I wouldn't even get any lard or leftover soup. If I kill it on the fifteenth of the seventh month, and sell it door-to-door in the nearby villages, one catty at a time, the money would be immediate. Ancestral sacrifices are held on the fifteenth of the seventh month, and every family needs some meat. I wouldn't have to worry about not selling it all. I'd keep the pig's head, lungs, intestines… the whole family would get to grease their mouths…"

Qinggen the Leper's calculations were correct. At the end of the seventh month, the ancestral hall would collect interest, and at the beginning of the eighth month, the hui loan would be repaid. It all depended on the output of this pig. All his hopes were pinned on this dark pigpen. Usually, he would rather tighten his belt a little, but the pig feed always had to be fed. He would sell people's grain to buy pig feed—soybean cake, chaff—why? To pay off his debt! Qinggen the Leper and his wife were not lazy, but they were flattened by "debt," unable to raise their heads. He himself didn't know what "old debt" he owed Grandpa A'hu. It was said that it was still the rent that his father had owed before his death. If he didn't admit it, Grandpa A'hu was the one who had the power to speak on the land. Who would dare to utter a "no"! Therefore, recently, Qinggen the Leper had become even more worried about the fat pig in the pen. He didn't even have those laughing dreams at night anymore.

However, some people still said happily to Qinggen the Leper, "Leper, you're lucky this year, raising such a fat pig." In fact, these words would only make him want to cry when he heard them. Wasn't that right, Grandpa A'hu had also told him to his face: if the thirteenth isn't paid in full, he would come to weigh the pig early on the fourteenth. He wouldn't let him kill the meat to sell on the fifteenth of the seventh month. Don't even think about greasing your mouth with the pig's head. Not even a single pig bristle would be left. Qinggen the Leper had bowed and knelt to him, but it was completely useless. That night, Qinggen had another laughing dream, jerking upright from the bed:

"What are you saying, what are you saying? Can't a poor person even have a fat pig? What are you saying? I raised the pig with half a year of effort. It ate my grain… you're going to drag it away and eat the meat as it is? Hehehe, you're taking my life, you're eating my flesh… are poor people only doomed to never get ahead?" This made Qinggen the Leper's wife start nagging again: "You miserable wretch, you're dragging your illness around, who are you scaring?"…

On the Ancient City Wall

—

In that ancient city, quietly lying in the southern wilderness, with a melancholy and aged appearance, I once spent seven different autumns. The changes in life are truly beyond your expectations: in that year, the middle school I was studying at was burned down in a sudden, thunderous change. After the incident calmed down, I no longer needed to walk that cement road to the outside of the north gate every day, waiting for the next semester to begin and continue my studies.

To maintain the safety of the county seat, a full regiment of soldiers was stationed there. Every time I went outside, the grey-clothed animals would always appear before my eyes. It was early autumn: the twilight of the southern autumn was endearing. I would often walk up the ancient city wall in such twilight, sitting alone, sitting, gradually becoming a habit. The twilight on the ancient city wall was truly so gentle and quiet. The sky was deep grey, and the sun had disappeared behind the mountain at some unknown time. Looking to the north, there was a field of mature crops, the ears of wheat swaying in the wind, like a sea of waves. The autumn wind was bringing coolness, and looking at the people walking slowly between the fields, I silently wished them well in my heart. Scattered across the fields were a few families' houses, the distant ones simply becoming small squares, with a wisp of smoke rising from them. In the south, the scenery was completely different, with rows of houses and shops, densely piled together into an ancient city. From time to time, I could hear the clamorous sounds of the market, presenting the inner workings of an increasingly complex commercial society. At such times, I would often hear the bugle calls for assembly or dismissal from the military camp, the metallic bugle calls often reminding me that it was late and I should go home for dinner, but I always lingered until it was completely dark…

Not far from my home, there was a troop of stationed soldiers. Because I went there a few times, I became acquainted with a company commander.

This young company commander was gentle and refined, unlike the rough characters of ordinary soldiers. His courteousness caught my attention. Once, I invited him out to sit and talk on the ancient city wall, and he happily agreed. (To be continued)
